remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mainstream_Christianity" title="Mainstream Christianity">Mainstream Christianity</a> professes belief in the <a href="/wiki/Nicene_Creed" title="Nicene Creed">Nicene Creed</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/English_versions_of_the_Nicene_Creed_in_current_use" title="English versions of the Nicene Creed in current use">English versions of the Nicene Creed in current use</a> include the phrase: "We look for the resurrection of the dead, and the life of the world to come."
</p><p>When questioned by the <a href="/wiki/Sadducees" title="Sadducees">Sadducees</a> about the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Resurrection_of_the_dead" title="Resurrection of the dead">resurrection of the dead</a> (in a context relating to who one's spouse would be if one had been married several times in life), <a href="/wiki/Jesus" title="Jesus">Jesus</a> said that marriage will be irrelevant after the resurrection as the resurrected will be like the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angels" title="Angels">angels</a> in heaven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup>
</p><p>Jesus also maintained that the time would come when the dead would hear the voice of the <a href="/wiki/Son_of_God" title="Son of God">Son of God</a>, and all who were in the tombs would come out; those who have heard His "[commandments] and believes in the one who sent [Him]" to the resurrection of life, but those who do not to the resurrection of condemnation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Enoch" title="Book of Enoch">Book of Enoch</a> describes Sheol as divided into four compartments for four types of the dead: the faithful saints who await resurrection in <a href="/wiki/Paradise" title="Paradise">Paradise</a>, the merely virtuous who await their reward, the wicked who await punishment, and the wicked who have already been punished and will not be resurrected on Judgment Day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The Book of Enoch is considered apocryphal by most denominations of Christianity and all denominations of Judaism.
</p><p>The book of <a href="/wiki/2_Maccabees" title="2 Maccabees">2 Maccabees</a> gives a clear account of the dead awaiting a future resurrection and judgment in addition to prayers and offerings for the dead to remove the burden of sin.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Domenico_Beccafumi_056.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2473" data-file-width="2024" decoding="async" height="269" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Domenico_Beccafumi_056.jpg/220px-Domenico_Beccafumi_056.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Domenico_Beccafumi_056.jpg/330px-Domenico_Beccafumi_056.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Domenico_Beccafumi_056.jpg/440px-Domenico_Beccafumi_056.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Domenico_Beccafumi_056.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Domenico_Beccafumi" title="Domenico Beccafumi">Domenico Beccafumi</a>'s <i>Inferno</i>: a Christian vision of hell</div></div></div>
<p>The author of <a href="/wiki/Gospel_of_Luke" title="Gospel of Luke">Luke</a> recounts the story of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lazarus_and_Dives" title="Lazarus and Dives">Lazarus and the rich man</a>, which shows people in Hades awaiting the resurrection either in comfort or torment. The author of the <a href="/wiki/Book_of_Revelation" title="Book of Revelation">Book of Revelation</a> writes about God and the angels versus <a href="/wiki/Satan" title="Satan">Satan</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Demons" title="Demons">demons</a> in an epic battle at the end of times when all souls are judged. There is mention of ghostly bodies of past prophets, and the <a href="/wiki/Transfiguration_of_Jesus" title="Transfiguration of Jesus">transfiguration</a>.
</p><p>The non-canonical <a href="/wiki/Acts_of_Paul_and_Thecla" title="Acts of Paul and Thecla">Acts of Paul and Thecla</a> speak of the efficacy of <a href="/wiki/Prayer_for_the_dead" title="Prayer for the dead">prayer for the dead</a> so that they might be "translated to a state of happiness".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Hippolytus_of_Rome" title="Hippolytus of Rome">Hippolytus of Rome</a> pictures the <a href="/wiki/Underworld" title="Underworld">underworld</a> (<a href="/wiki/Greek_underworld" title="Greek underworld">Hades</a>) as a place where the righteous dead, awaiting in the <a href="/wiki/Bosom_of_Abraham" title="Bosom of Abraham">bosom of Abraham</a> their resurrection, rejoice at their future prospect, while the unrighteous are tormented at the sight of the "<a href="/wiki/Lake_of_fire" title="Lake of fire">lake of unquenchable fire</a>" into which they are destined to be cast.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Gregory_of_Nyssa" title="Gregory of Nyssa">Gregory of Nyssa</a> discusses the long-before believed possibility of purification of souls after death.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup>
</p><p>Pope Gregory I repeats the concept, articulated over a century earlier by <a href="/wiki/Gregory_of_Nyssa" title="Gregory of Nyssa">Gregory of Nyssa</a> that the saved suffer purification after death, in connection with which he wrote of "purgatorial flames".
</p><p>The noun <a href="/wiki/Purgatory" title="Purgatory">"purgatorium"</a> (Latin: place of cleansing<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup>) is used for the first time to describe a state of painful purification of the saved after life. The same word in adjectival form (<i>purgatorius -a -um</i>, cleansing), which appears also in non-religious writing,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> was already used by Christians such as Augustine of Hippo and <a href="/wiki/Pope_Gregory_I" title="Pope Gregory I">Pope Gregory I</a> to refer to an after-death cleansing.
</p><p>During the <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Age of Enlightenment</a>, theologians and philosophers presented various philosophies and beliefs. A notable example is <a href="/wiki/Emanuel_Swedenborg" title="Emanuel Swedenborg">Emanuel Swedenborg</a> who wrote some 18 theological works which describe in detail the nature of the afterlife according to his claimed spiritual experiences, the most famous of which is <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heaven_and_Hell_(Swedenborg)" title="Heaven and Hell (Swedenborg)">Heaven and Hell</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-swedenborgdigitallibrary.org_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-swedenborgdigitallibrary.org-51">[51]</a></sup> His report of life there covers a wide range of topics, such as <a href="/wiki/Marriage" title="Marriage">marriage</a> in heaven (where all <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angels" title="Angels">angels</a> are married), children in heaven (where they are raised by angel parents), <a href="/wiki/Time" title="Time">time</a> and <a href="/wiki/Space" title="Space">space</a> in heaven (there are none), the after-death awakening process in the World of Spirits (a place halfway between Heaven and Hell and where people first wake up after death), the allowance of a free will choice between Heaven or Hell (as opposed to being sent to either one by God), the <a href="/wiki/Eternity" title="Eternity">eternity</a> of <a href="/wiki/Hell" title="Hell">Hell</a> (one could leave but would never want to), and that all angels or devils were once people on earth.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-swedenborgdigitallibrary.org_51-1"><a href="#cite_note-swedenborgdigitallibrary.org-51">[51]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Catholic_Church">The Catholic Church</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afterlife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: The Catholic Church">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Catholic conception of the afterlife teaches that <a href="/wiki/Particular_judgment" title="Particular judgment">after the body dies, the soul is judged</a>, the righteous and free of sin enter Heaven. However, those who die in unrepented <a href="/wiki/Mortal_sin" title="Mortal sin">mortal sin</a> go to hell. In the 1990s, the <a href="/wiki/Catechism_of_the_Catholic_Church" title="Catechism of the Catholic Church">Catechism of the Catholic Church</a> defined hell not as punishment imposed on the sinner but rather as the sinner's self-exclusion from God. Unlike other Christian groups, the Catholic Church teaches that those who die in a state of grace, but still carry <a href="/wiki/Venial_sin" title="Venial sin">venial sin</a>, go to a place called <a href="/wiki/Purgatory" title="Purgatory">Purgatory</a> where they undergo purification to enter Heaven.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Limbo">Limbo</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afterlife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Limbo">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Limbo" title="Limbo">Limbo</a></div>
<p>Despite popular opinion, Limbo, which was elaborated upon by theologians beginning in the Middle Ages, was never recognized as a <a href="/wiki/Dogma" title="Dogma">dogma</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>, yet, at times, it has been a very popular theological theory within the Church. Limbo is a theory that unbaptized but innocent souls, such as those of infants, <a href="/wiki/Virtue#Christianity" title="Virtue">virtuous</a> individuals who lived before <a href="/wiki/Nativity_of_Jesus" title="Nativity of Jesus">Jesus Christ was born on earth</a>, or those that die before <a href="/wiki/Baptism" title="Baptism">baptism</a> exist in neither Heaven nor Hell proper. Therefore, these souls neither merit the <a href="/wiki/Beatific_vision" title="Beatific vision">beatific vision</a>, nor are subjected to any punishment, because they are not guilty of any personal <a href="/wiki/Sin" title="Sin">sin</a> although they have not received baptism, so still bear <a href="/wiki/Original_sin" title="Original sin">original sin</a>. So they are generally seen as existing in a state of natural, but not supernatural, happiness, until the end of time.
</p><p>In other <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christian_denominations" title="Christian denominations">Christian denominations</a> it has been described as an <a href="/wiki/Intermediate_state" title="Intermediate state">intermediate place</a> or state of confinement in oblivion and neglect.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Purgatory">Purgatory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afterlife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Purgatory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Purgatory" title="Purgatory">Purgatory</a></div>
<p>The notion of <a href="/wiki/Purgatory" title="Purgatory">purgatory</a> is associated particularly with the <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">Catholic Church</a>. In the Catholic Church, all those who die in God's grace and friendship, but still imperfectly purified, are indeed assured of their eternal salvation; but after death they undergo purification, so as to achieve the holiness necessary to enter the joy of heaven or the final purification of the elect, which is entirely different from the punishment of the damned. The tradition of the church, by reference to certain texts of scripture, speaks of a "cleansing fire" although it is not always called purgatory.
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglican" title="Anglican">Anglicans</a> of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anglo-Catholic" title="Anglo-Catholic">Anglo-Catholic</a> tradition generally also hold to the belief. <a href="/wiki/John_Wesley" title="John Wesley">John Wesley</a>, the founder of <a href="/wiki/Methodism" title="Methodism">Methodism</a>, believed in an <a href="/wiki/Intermediate_state" title="Intermediate state">intermediate state</a> between death and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Resurrection_of_the_dead" title="Resurrection of the dead">resurrection of the dead</a> and in the possibility of "continuing to grow in holiness there", but Methodism does not officially affirm this belief and denies the possibility of <a href="/wiki/Prayer_for_the_dead" title="Prayer for the dead">helping by prayer</a> any who may be in that state.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Orthodox_Christianity">Orthodox Christianity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afterlife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Orthodox Christianity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Orthodox Church is intentionally reticent on the afterlife, as it acknowledges the mystery especially of things that have not yet occurred.  Beyond the second coming of Jesus, bodily resurrection, and final judgment, all of which is affirmed in the <a href="/wiki/Nicene_Creed" title="Nicene Creed">Nicene Creed</a> (325 CE), Orthodoxy does not teach much else in any definitive manner.  Unlike Western forms of Christianity, however, Orthodoxy is traditionally non-dualist and does not teach that there are two separate literal locations of heaven and hell, but instead acknowledges that "the 'location' of one's final destiny—heaven or hell—as being figurative."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Andrew_P._Klager_2011_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Andrew_P._Klager_2011-54">[54]</a></sup>
</p><p>Instead, Orthodoxy teaches that the final judgment is simply one's uniform encounter with divine love and mercy, but this encounter is experienced multifariously depending on the extent to which one has been transformed, partaken of divinity, and is therefore compatible or incompatible with God. "The monadic, immutable, and ceaseless object of eschatological encounter is therefore the love and mercy of God, his glory which infuses the heavenly temple, and it is the subjective human reaction which engenders multiplicity or any division of experience."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Andrew_P._Klager_2011_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-Andrew_P._Klager_2011-54">[54]</a></sup> For instance, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Isaac_the_Syrian" title="St. Isaac the Syrian">St. Isaac the Syrian</a> observes that "those who are punished in Gehenna, are scourged by the scourge of love. ... The power of love works in two ways: it torments sinners ... [as] bitter regret. But love inebriates the souls of the sons of Heaven by its delectability."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In this sense, the divine action is always, immutably, and uniformly love and if one experiences this love negatively, the experience is then one of self-condemnation because of free will rather than condemnation by God.
</p><p>Orthodoxy therefore uses the description of Jesus' judgment in John 3:19–21 as their model: "19 And this is the judgment: the light has come into the world, and people loved the darkness rather than the light because their works were evil. 20 For everyone who does wicked things hates the light and does not come to the light, lest his works should be exposed. 21 But whoever does what is true comes to the light, so that it may be clearly seen that his works have been carried out in God." As a characteristically Orthodox understanding, then, Fr. <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Hopko" title="Thomas Hopko">Thomas Hopko</a> writes, "[I]t is precisely the presence of God's mercy and love which cause the torment of the wicked. God does not punish; he forgives... . In a word, God has mercy on all, whether all like it or not. If we like it, it is paradise; if we do not, it is hell. Every knee will bend before the Lord. Everything will be subject to Him. God in Christ will indeed be "all and in all," with boundless mercy and unconditional pardon. But not all will rejoice in God's gift of forgiveness, and that choice will be judgment, the self-inflicted source of their sorrow and pain."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>
</p><p>Moreover, Orthodoxy includes a prevalent tradition of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apokatastasis" title="Apokatastasis">apokatastasis</a></i>, or the restoration of all things in the end. This has been taught most notably by <a href="/wiki/Origen" title="Origen">Origen</a>, but also many other Church fathers and Saints, including <a href="/wiki/Gregory_of_Nyssa" title="Gregory of Nyssa">Gregory of Nyssa</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Second_Council_of_Constantinople" title="Second Council of Constantinople">Second Council of Constantinople</a> (553 CE) affirmed the orthodoxy of Gregory of Nyssa while simultaneously condemning Origen's brand of universalism because it taught the restoration back to our pre-existent state, which Orthodoxy doesn't teach.  It is also a teaching of such eminent Orthodox theologians as <a href="/wiki/Olivier_Cl%C3%A9ment" title="Olivier Clément">Olivier Clément</a>, Metropolitan <a href="/wiki/Kallistos_Ware" title="Kallistos Ware">Kallistos Ware</a>, and Bishop <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hilarion_Alfeyev" title="Hilarion Alfeyev">Hilarion Alfeyev</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> Although apokatastasis is not a dogma of the church but instead a <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/theologoumenon#English" title="wikt:theologoumenon">theologoumenon</a>, it is no less a teaching of the Orthodox Church than its rejection.  As Met. Kallistos Ware explains, "It is heretical to say that all must be saved, for this is to deny free will; but, it is legitimate to hope that all may be saved,"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> as insisting on torment without end also denies free will.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afterlife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Plan_of_salvation_(Latter_Day_Saints)" title="Plan of salvation (Latter Day Saints)">Plan of salvation (Latter Day Saints)</a>, <a href="/wiki/Exaltation_(Mormonism)" title="Exaltation (Mormonism)">Exaltation (Mormonism)</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Degrees_of_glory" title="Degrees of glory">Degrees of glory</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:000_preach-my-gospel_1207575_tmb.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="92" data-file-width="450" decoding="async" height="92" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/a5/000_preach-my-gospel_1207575_tmb.jpg" width="450"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption">Plan of Salvation in LDS Religion</div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Joseph_F._Smith" title="Joseph F. Smith">Joseph F. Smith</a> of <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> presents an elaborate vision of the afterlife. It is revealed as the scene of an extensive missionary effort by righteous spirits in paradise to redeem those still in darkness—a spirit prison or "hell" where the spirits of the dead remain until judgment. It is divided into two parts: Spirit Prison and Paradise. Together these are also known as the Spirit World (also Abraham's Bosom; see Luke 16:19–25). They believe that Christ visited spirit prison <a class="external text" href="https://www.churchofjesuschrist.org/study/scriptures/nt/1-pet/3.18-20?lang=eng" rel="nofollow">(1 Peter 3:18–20)</a> and opened the gate for those who repent to cross over to Paradise. This is similar to the <a href="/wiki/Harrowing_of_Hell" title="Harrowing of Hell">Harrowing of Hell</a> doctrine of some mainstream Christian faiths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Both Spirit Prison and Paradise are temporary according to Latter-day Saint beliefs. After the resurrection, spirits are assigned "permanently" to three degrees of heavenly glory, determined by how they lived – Celestial, Terrestrial, and Telestial. (1 Cor 15:44–42; Doctrine and Covenants, Section 76) <a href="/wiki/Son_of_perdition_(Mormonism)" title="Son of perdition (Mormonism)">Sons of Perdition</a>, or those who have known and seen God and deny it, will be sent to the realm of <a href="/wiki/Satan" title="Satan">Satan</a>, which is called Outer Darkness, where they shall live in misery and agony forever.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> However, according to the beliefs of the Church of Jesus Christ of Latter Day Saints, most persons lack the amount of knowledge to commit the <a href="/wiki/Eternal_sin" title="Eternal sin">Eternal sin</a> and are therefore incapable of becoming sons of perdition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup>
</p><p>The Celestial Kingdom is believed to be a place where the righteous can live eternally with their families. Progression does not end once one has entered the Celestial Kingdom, but extends eternally. According to "True to the Faith" (a handbook on doctrines in the LDS faith), "The celestial kingdom is the place prepared for those who have "received the testimony of Jesus" and been "made perfect through Jesus the mediator of the new covenant, who wrought out this perfect atonement through the shedding of his own blood" (Doctrine and Covenants, 76:51, 69). To inherit this gift, we must receive the ordinances of salvation, keep the commandments, and repent of our sins."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Jehovah.27s_Witnesses"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Jehovah's_Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afterlife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Jehovah's Witnesses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a> occasionally use terms such as "afterlife"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> to refer to any hope for the dead, but they understand <a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastes" title="Ecclesiastes">Ecclesiastes</a> 9:5 to preclude belief in an immortal soul.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> Individuals judged by God to be wicked, such as in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Flood" title="Great Flood">Great Flood</a> or at <a href="/wiki/Armageddon" title="Armageddon">Armageddon</a>, are given no hope of an afterlife. However, they believe that after Armageddon there will be a bodily resurrection of "both righteous and unrighteous" dead (but not the "wicked"). Survivors of Armageddon and those who are resurrected are then to gradually restore earth to a paradise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> After Armageddon, unrepentant sinners are punished with eternal death (non-existence).
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Seventh-day_Adventists">Seventh-day Adventists</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afterlife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Seventh-day Adventists">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Life_And_Death_Equation.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="1100" decoding="async" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Life_And_Death_Equation.jpg/220px-Life_And_Death_Equation.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Life_And_Death_Equation.jpg/330px-Life_And_Death_Equation.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Life_And_Death_Equation.jpg/440px-Life_And_Death_Equation.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Life_And_Death_Equation.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Creation and Death Equation</div></div></div>
<p>The Seventh-day Adventist Church's beliefs regarding the afterlife differ from other Christian churches. Rather than ascend to Heaven or descend to Hell, Adventists believe the dead "remain unconscious until the return of Christ in judgement". The concept that the dead remain dead until resurrection is one of the fundamental beliefs of Seventh-day Adventist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> Adventists believe that death is an unconscious state (a "sleep"). This is based on Matt. 9:24; Mark 5:39; John 11:11-14; 1 Cor. 15:51, 52; 1 Thess. 4:13-17; 2 Peter 3:4; Eccl. 9:5, 6, 10. At death, all consciousness ends. The dead person does not know anything and does not do anything.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> They believe that death is creation, only in reverse. Ecclesiastes 12:7. When a person dies, the body turns to dust again, and the spirit goes back to God, who gave it. The spirit of every person who dies—whether saved or unsaved—returns to God at death. The spirit that returns to God at death is the breath of life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Islam">Islam</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afterlife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Islam">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Islamic_view_of_death" title="Islamic view of death">Islamic view of death</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Akhirah" title="Akhirah">Akhirah</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barzakh" title="Barzakh">Barzakh</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Punishment_of_the_Grave" title="Punishment of the Grave">Punishment of the Grave</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mohammed%C2%B4s_Paradise.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="648" data-file-width="401" decoding="async" height="323" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Mohammed%C2%B4s_Paradise.jpg/200px-Mohammed%C2%B4s_Paradise.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Mohammed%C2%B4s_Paradise.jpg/300px-Mohammed%C2%B4s_Paradise.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Mohammed%C2%B4s_Paradise.jpg/400px-Mohammed%C2%B4s_Paradise.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mohammed%C2%B4s_Paradise.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An artist's representation of "Muhammed's Paradise" with its seven levels. <a href="/wiki/Persian_miniature" title="Persian miniature">Persian miniature</a> from <i>The History of Mohammed</i> (1808), <a href="/wiki/Biblioth%C3%A8que_nationale_de_France" title="Bibliothèque nationale de France">Bibliothèque nationale de France</a>, Paris.</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Quran</a> (the holy book of Islam), emphasizes the insignificance of worldly life (<i>ḥayāt ad-dunyā</i> usually translated as "this world") vis-a-vis the hereafter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[Note 1]</a></sup>
A central doctrine of Islamic faith is <a href="/wiki/Last_Judgment#In_Islam" title="Last Judgment">the Last Day</a> (<i>al-yawm al-ākhir</i>, also known by other names),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[Note 2]</a></sup> on which the world will come to an end and God will raise all mankind (as well as the <i><a href="/wiki/Jinn" title="Jinn">jinn</a></i>) from the dead and evaluate their worldly actions. The resurrected will be judged according to their deeds,  records of which are kept on two books compiled for every human being—one for their good deeds and one for their evil ones.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-72">[70]</a></sup>
</p><p>Having been judged, the resurrected will cross the bridge of <a href="/wiki/As-Sir%C4%81t" title="As-Sirāt">As-Sirāt</a> over the pit of hell; when the condemned attempt to they will be made to fall off into hellfire below; while the righteous will have no trouble and continue on to their eternal abode of heaven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leviton_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-Leviton-73">[71]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Idris_the_prophet.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="606" data-file-width="389" decoding="async" height="312" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Idris_the_prophet.jpg/200px-Idris_the_prophet.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e2/Idris_the_prophet.jpg/300px-Idris_the_prophet.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e2/Idris_the_prophet.jpg 2x" width="200"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Idris_the_prophet.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A depiction of <a href="/wiki/Idris_(prophet)" title="Idris (prophet)">Idris</a> visiting Heaven and Hell from an <a href="/wiki/Illuminated_manuscript" title="Illuminated manuscript">illuminated manuscript</a> version of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stories_of_the_Prophets" title="Stories of the Prophets">Stories of the Prophets</a></i> (1577).</div></div></div> <div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:292px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Muhammad_and_%22shameless_women%22_in_Hell.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="417" data-file-width="504" decoding="async" height="240" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Muhammad_and_%22shameless_women%22_in_Hell.jpg/290px-Muhammad_and_%22shameless_women%22_in_Hell.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Muhammad_and_%22shameless_women%22_in_Hell.jpg/435px-Muhammad_and_%22shameless_women%22_in_Hell.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2c/Muhammad_and_%22shameless_women%22_in_Hell.jpg 2x" width="290"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Muhammad_and_%22shameless_women%22_in_Hell.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buraq" title="Buraq">Buraq</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gabriel" title="Gabriel">Gabriel</a> observe "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prostitution_in_Islam" title="Prostitution in Islam">shameless women</a>" being punished in Hell.</div></div></div>
<p>Afterlife in Islam actually begins before the Last Day.
After death, humans will be questioned about their faith by two angels, <a href="/wiki/Munkar_and_Nakir" title="Munkar and Nakir">Munkar and Nakīr</a>.  Those who die as martyrs go immediately to paradise.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Britannica_72-1"><a href="#cite_note-Britannica-72">[70]</a></sup> Others who have died and been buried, will receive a taste of their eternal reward from the <i>al-qabr</i> or "the grave" (compare the <a href="#Judaism">Jewish concept</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sheol" title="Sheol">Sheol</a>). Those bound for hell will suffer "<a href="/wiki/Punishment_of_the_Grave" title="Punishment of the Grave">punishment of the grave</a>", while those bound for heaven will find the grave "peaceful and blessed".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-JACBMM2014:46_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-JACBMM2014:46-74">[72]</a></sup>
</p><p>Islamic scripture — the <a href="/wiki/Quran" title="Quran">Quran</a>  and <a href="/wiki/Hadith" title="Hadith">hadith</a> (reports of the words and deeds of the Islamic Prophet <a href="/wiki/Muhammad" title="Muhammad">Muhammad</a> who is believed to have visited heaven and hell during his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isra_and_Mi%27raj" title="Isra and Mi'raj">Isra and Mi'raj</a> journey) -- give vivid descriptions of the pleasures of paradise (<a href="/wiki/Jannah" title="Jannah">Jannah</a>) and sufferings of hell (<i><a href="/wiki/Jahannam" title="Jahannam">Jahannam</a></i>). The gardens of jannah have cool shade  <sup>[Quran <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/36?startingVerse=56" rel="nofollow">36:56-57</a>]</sup> adorned couchs and cushions  <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/18?startingVerse=31" rel="nofollow">18:31</a>]</sup>  rich carpets spread out,  cups  <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/88?startingVerse=10" rel="nofollow">88:10-16</a>]</sup> full of wine  <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/52?startingVerse=23" rel="nofollow">52:23</a>]</sup> and every meat  <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/52?startingVerse=22" rel="nofollow">52:22</a>]</sup> and fruit  <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/36?startingVerse=56" rel="nofollow">36:56-57</a>]</sup>. Men will be provided with perpetually youthful, beautiful <i><a href="/wiki/Houri" title="Houri">ḥūr</a></i>, "untouched beforehand by man or jinn",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rustomji_2017_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rustomji_2017-75">[73]</a></sup> <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/55?startingVerse=56" rel="nofollow">55:56</a>]</sup> with large, beautiful eyes  <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/37?startingVerse=48" rel="nofollow">37:48</a>]</sup>.
(In recent years some have argued that the term <i>ḥūr</i> refers both to pure men and pure women,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dawn-houri-20_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-dawn-houri-20-76">[74]</a></sup> and/or that Quranic references to "immortal boys" ( <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/56?startingVerse=17" rel="nofollow">56:17</a>,  <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/76?startingVerse=19" rel="nofollow">76:19</a>) or "young men" ( <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/52?startingVerse=24" rel="nofollow">52:24</a>) (<i><a href="/wiki/Ghilman" title="Ghilman">ghilmān</a></i>, <i>wildān</i>, and <i>suqāh</i>) who serve <a href="/wiki/Wine#Islam" title="Wine">wine</a> and meals to the <a href="/wiki/Blessing#Islam" title="Blessing">blessed</a>, are the male equivalents of hur.)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rustomji_2017_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-Rustomji_2017-75">[73]</a></sup>
</p><p>In contrast, those in <a href="/wiki/Jahannam" title="Jahannam">Jahannam</a> will dwell in a land infested with thousands of serpents and scorpions;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[75]</a></sup> be "burnt" by "scorching fire"  <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/88?startingVerse=1" rel="nofollow">88:1-7</a>]</sup> and when "their skins are roasted through, We shall change them for fresh skins" to repeat the process forever  <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/4?startingVerse=56" rel="nofollow">4:56</a>]</sup>; they will have nothing to drink but "boiling water and running sores"  <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/78?startingVerse=21" rel="nofollow">78:21-30</a>]</sup>;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hughes-DoI_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-hughes-DoI-78">[76]</a></sup>   their cries of remorse and pleading for forgiveness will be in vain  <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/26?startingVerse=96" rel="nofollow">26:96-106</a>]</sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ItQ-233_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-ItQ-233-79">[77]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[78]</a></sup>
</p><p>Traditionally <i>jannah</i> and <i>jahannam</i> are thought to have different levels.  Eight gates and eight levels in <i>Jannah</i>, where the higher the level the better it is and the happier you are. <i>Jahannam</i> possess seven layers. Each layer more horrible than the one above.
</p><p>The Quran teaches that the purpose of Man's creation is to worship God and God alone.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[Note 3]</a></sup> Those it describes as being punished in hell are "most typically",  unbelievers, including those who worship others besides Allah  <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/10?startingVerse=24" rel="nofollow">10:24</a>]</sup>, those who deny the divine origin of the Quran  <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/74?startingVerse=16" rel="nofollow">74:16-26</a>]</sup>, or the coming of Judgement Day  <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/25?startingVerse=11" rel="nofollow">25:11-14</a>]</sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ETISN2009_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-ETISN2009-83">[80]</a></sup><sup class="reference nowrap"><span title="Page / location: 404">: 404 </span></sup>
</p><p>Straightforward crimes/sins against other people are also grounds for going to hell: the murder of a believer  <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/4?startingVerse=93" rel="nofollow">4:93</a>]</sup> <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/3?startingVerse=21" rel="nofollow">3:21</a>]</sup>, usury (Q.2:275) <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/2?startingVerse=275" rel="nofollow">2:275</a>]</sup>, devouring the property of an orphan  <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/4?startingVerse=10" rel="nofollow">4:10</a>]</sup>, slander  <sup>[Quran <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/104?startingVerse=" rel="nofollow">104:</a>]</sup>, particularly of a chaste woman  <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/24?startingVerse=23" rel="nofollow">24:23</a>]</sup>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ETISN2009:405_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-ETISN2009:405-84">[81]</a></sup>
However it is a common belief among Muslims that whatever crimes/sins Muslims may have committed, their punishment in hell will be temporary. Only unbelievers will reside in hell permanently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-85">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[Note 4]</a></sup> Thus Jahannam combines both the concept of an eternal hell (for unbelievers), and what is known in Christian Catholicism as <a href="/wiki/Purgatory" title="Purgatory">purgatory</a> (for believers eventually destined for heaven after punishment for their sins).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[85]</a></sup>
</p><p>The common belief holds that <i>Jahannam</i> coexists with the temporal world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Islamic_Traditions_p._12_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-Islamic_Traditions_p._12-90">[86]</a></sup> Mainstream Islam teaches the continued existence of the soul and a transformed physical existence after death. The resurrection that will take place on the Last Day is physical, and is explained by suggesting that God will re-create the decayed body ("Have they not realized that Allah, Who created the heavens and the earth, can ˹easily˺ re-create them?"  <sup>[ <a class="external text" href="https://quran.com/17?startingVerse=99" rel="nofollow">17:99</a>]</sup>).
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Ahmadiyya">Ahmadiyya</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Afterlife&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Ahmadiyya">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>

<div class="sidebar-list mw-collapsible mw-collapsed"><div class="sidebar-list-title">Miscellaneous</div><div class="sidebar-list-content mw-collapsible-content hlist">
